Lawyer Zhang Shizhao Returns to Shanghai 110

Discussing the Handling of the Chen Peng Case Without Any Taboos

Also Praising Judicial Progress and Government Magnanimity

Lawyer Zhang Shizhao went to Beijing to handle the Chen Peng case, and the debate has ended. He returned to Shanghai yesterday. Because this case has caused a stir among the world, reporters paid a special visit to ask about the circumstances of the court hearing and to ask for his observations for reference. He said that this case is the biggest case in recent times. In the 20th year of the Republic, those who committed political suspicion, similar to Chen Peng, mostly died illegally. The Li Dazhao case and the Gao Renshan case are still in the memory of the Chinese people. Open trial and permission for defense lawyers to formally defend in court, this case should be considered the first time. This can indeed be seen as judicial progress, and the national government's magnanimity is very admirable. In his court defense, he was based on legal principles and referenced facts, and he said whatever he wanted to say, without any taboos. He secretly worried that he might have offended the government in some way, but when he left the court, a reporter from the Central News Agency firmly took the original manuscript away. The original text was not altered in the slightest, and the entire article was published in the Central Daily News. He met with important figures in the party, and they all praised him without any different opinions. It can be seen that the people who use the government's oppression of public opinion as an excuse and are silent are overly concerned and their assessment of the government's mentality is not accurate. It is unfair to let the government bear the name of slaughtering and humiliating scholars. At this time of national crisis, regardless of the government or the people, they should eliminate fraud and start from the strengths of others. The government's attitude towards the Chen case is open and upright, and he admires it very much. By analogy, why worry that the country will not see the light of day? Because the statements are relevant, they are recorded as right.

(Welcome by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs) Luo Wengan, the Minister of Foreign Affairs, has appointed Mr. Li Dijun, the Director of the Information Department of the Ministry, as a representative to welcome Mr. Bogomolov, the Russian Ambassador, to show the friendship between the two countries. He arrived in port yesterday morning and has agreed on the welcome procedures with Mr. Zhao Tiezhang, the Acting Director of the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. It is said that our authorities will not hold any welcome ceremonies after Mr. Bogomolov arrives in Shanghai.

(Scheduled Trip to the Capital) According to Russian emigrant sources, after arriving in Shanghai, Mr. Bogomolov will temporarily reside at the Cathay Hotel, and the rest of the entourage will reside in the Nanyuan Building at No. 1607 Xinzha Road. Mr. Bogomolov will stay in Shanghai for about two weeks, and then go to Beijing to meet with Chairman Lin to present his credentials.

Yutong Ship Came to Shanghai After Trouble 117

Escorted by a Japanese Ship Yesterday to Shen

Subsequently Entered the Jiangnan Shipyard for Repair

The Yutong ship of the Yu Da Company ran aground on a reef near Gao Bei Mountain in Xinghua, Fujian on the 24th of last month. The insurance company hired a Japanese salvage company to try to save it. The salvage ship Arerumaru was dispatched from Moji to the scene of the accident to assist. This was recorded in previous reports. It has been a month since then. It is now learned that the ship was rescued by the Japanese ship, which first removed the cargo from the cabin, floated the ship, and then repaired the holes in the first two cabins. It was then towed to Xinghua for major repairs. Fortunately, the ship's machinery was not damaged. Therefore, the ship was escorted to Shanghai by a Japanese ship from Xinghua. It safely entered the port at 10:00 a.m. yesterday and immediately sailed into the Jiangnan Shipyard. It is scheduled to be inspected tomorrow and then repairs will begin. It is heard that in this accident, in addition to the ship's hull being punctured and most of the passengers and cargo being lost, the crew were completely safe, which is a great stroke of luck in misfortune.

The Navigation Administration Will Set Up an Arbitration Council 118

The Inspection of Foreign Ships Has Not Yet Yielded Results

A reporter from the Central News Agency visited Zhu Yaoting, the Director of the Shanghai Navigation Administration of the Ministry of Communications, at the bureau yesterday morning to inquire about new measures for managing navigation administration. He said the following:

Inspection of Foreign Ships 119

In view of the fact that foreign ships traveling domestically have not been inspected by our side, which is a loss of national rights, the Ministry of Communications has previously ordered the navigation administrations in various places to conduct negotiations to be able to implement inspections in the near future. Since receiving the order, this bureau has repeatedly negotiated with foreign businesses, but has not achieved a complete result. However, small foreign ships have been inspected by our side. The major ships will have to wait for further negotiations before a decision can be made. I have presented the details to the ministry for instructions.

Maritime Safety 120

Our country has now joined the International Convention for the Safety of Life at Sea and will implement it on the 14th of next month. This bureau has received an order from the ministry. The preparations have been notified to various ship bureaus, and more attention should be paid to the safety of passenger ships.

Recovery of Navigation Rights 121

In recent years, foreign ships have freely traveled within our country, encroaching upon our inland river navigation rights. The Ministry of Transportation and the national shipping industry have all recognized the urgency of recovering inland river navigation rights. Therefore, active planning is underway to develop recovery methods. This will not only ensure the early recovery of seized sovereignty but also allow our national shipping industry to gradually develop.

Arbitration Committee 122

I have noted that unfortunate events, such as collisions between ships, are frequently reported. The occurrence of such unfortunate events not only endangers maritime safety but also leads to disputes over the subsequent arbitration of right and wrong. Historically, such disputes have been taken to court, and the courts often consult the Navigation Bureau regarding the circumstances of the incident. I believe that the Navigation Bureau, established to manage navigation affairs, should have an arbitration committee. Preparations are currently underway, and prominent figures from major shipping companies, as well as navigators and legal experts, will be invited to serve as committee members.

Expansion of the Shanghai Volunteer Corps 123

The *North-China Daily News* reports that the divisional reviews of the Shanghai Volunteer Corps in the International Settlement have now been completed. The progress regarding preparations for future mobilization is something that all members are eager to know. Since the many disturbances of last spring, the corps has experienced a number of difficulties and is currently working to remedy them. The foundation of the corps is three infantry companies. Although it is not yet time to adopt a battalion-level organization, this is the logical trend in infantry organization. In the future, these three companies may be expanded into three battalions. In addition, the various units can be divided into two categories, such as the Light Horse, the American Company, the Armored Car Company, and the Artillery Company, which may be used in areas with fewer restrictions than the infantry. Therefore, a centralized management approach will be adopted. However, in light of the difficulties experienced during last year's mobilization, one of the biggest causes was the excessive centralization of management. Therefore, in the future, where it does not lead to a loss of effectiveness, decentralization of management will be sought. As a result, minor changes will be made to the internal structure of the headquarters, such as building a new kitchen at the small target range. Currently, the corps has a total of twenty-three units, with members of different nationalities. According to the current organizational method, whenever a mobilization order is issued, the special function of each unit is to prepare for mobilization. The hope is that by the end of this year, each unit will have its own headquarters and mobilization supply room. A joint office will be established for every few units, so that in the future, members do not need to request everything from headquarters, thus avoiding delays. Furthermore, items such as military boots and rain hats are also being prepared to address previous shortcomings. Also, when the entire corps is deployed, there is a noticeable lack of personnel to handle routine back-office affairs. Work has now begun to organize a Reserve Company A, with the Commander-in-Chief adding technical training. In addition, the newly formed Air Defense Company of the corps held its second encampment during the Easter holiday, with training provided by British military instructors. As for the Western Boys' Student Corps, efforts are also being made to make progress, hoping to become a strong force.

Rectifying Lawyers' Ethics and Professional Conduct 132

Drafts of Pleadings Must Not Be Sent to Newspapers in Advance

Official Titles Must Not Be Displayed on Door Signs for Solicitation

The Shanghai Lawyers Association recently received instructions from the Jiangsu Shanghai First Special District Local Court, which stated: "Regarding the implementation of orders, we have received Order No. 397 from the Prosecutor of the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, which contains Order No. 945 from the Ministry of Justice. Lawyers are specially authorized by the state to represent or defend people in lawsuits. They should cultivate moral integrity internally and uphold respect externally. They should not engage in actions that are improper and invite criticism. Recently, we have heard that some lawyers draft pleadings for others, and either after submitting them or even before submitting them, they send the drafts to newspapers. The content of these lawsuits often contains embellished language, accusations, and extravagant descriptions that are not necessary for attack or defense in litigation, merely harming the reputation and credibility of the opposing party. If there is no ulterior motive, why would they do this? We have also heard that some lawyers who previously held public office display their former official titles in newspapers and on door signs, showing off themselves. With such a noble profession, why engage in the same practices as merchants, boasting and soliciting business? The above two points are closely related to the ethics and professional conduct of lawyers and must be clearly emphasized to warn future practitioners. Therefore, we order you to instruct the chief prosecutors of the courts under your jurisdiction to issue orders to the lawyer associations under their jurisdiction to strictly prohibit these practices to prevent abuses and dispel public criticism. This order is equivalent to this order. We hereby order you, the chief prosecutor, to order the lawyer association under your jurisdiction to strictly prohibit these practices. This order is equivalent to this order. We hereby order you, the lawyer association, to comply with this order." After receiving the order, the association submitted it to a joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committee members, who resolved to notify all members to strictly comply with the ministry's orders and prohibitions.

Deaf-Mute Murderer Sentenced 134

Zhao Genlin to Eight Years, Zhao Wenhao to Seven Years

Chen Hongcai, who runs a fruit store in Dongxing Lane, Minquan Road, hired Zhao Genlin as a clerk. Zhao has a volatile temper and often beats people. One day, a deaf-mute man named Chen Xuelu went to buy fruit, but because he could not speak clearly, he angered Zhao Genlin, who beat him. Zhao Wenhao, a former teacher, gave Zhao Genlin a sharp knife and incited him to violence, resulting in the mute man's left kidney being pierced. He died before he could be taken to the hospital. The Public Security Bureau arrested Zhao Genlin and Zhao Wenhao and handed them over to the local court. After prosecutor Yang An's thorough investigation, and with Zhao Genlin confessing that Zhao Wenhao had given him the knife to kill, it was determined that they had malicious intentions, and they were prosecuted. After being tried by Judge He Renji, they were sentenced yesterday. Zhao Genlin was sentenced to eight years of imprisonment, and Zhao Wenhao was sentenced to seven years of imprisonment as a warning.

The Shanghai Citizens' Association for Promoting National Goods Pays Attention to the Use of Enemy Goods by Handkerchief Factories 135

The Shanghai Citizens' Association for Promoting National Goods sent a letter to the Shanghai Handkerchief Industry Association yesterday: "Dear Sirs, according to a confidential report from a member, some handkerchief factories are using enemy goods in order to make a profit. Please investigate. During this time of national crisis and economic panic, it is outrageous for handkerchief factories to use enemy goods. It not only undermines the movement to promote national goods but also provides an opportunity for enemy goods to be dumped on the market. There are undoubtedly patriotic individuals in your industry, but if you continue to tolerate and harbor unscrupulous merchants and allow them to pass off enemy goods as national goods, it will tarnish your reputation. We hereby request your association to promptly send personnel to thoroughly investigate all factories and strictly prohibit the use of enemy goods in order to protect national goods and enhance your industry's reputation. We look forward to your response."

The Case of Yang Yao's Suicide by Poisoning - Corpse Still Needs to Be Autopsied 136

Yang Yao, a 21-year-old woman from Suzhou, residing at No. 133 Xiamen Road, had an argument with her husband, Yang Baofa, on the 19th of this month. She went to bed angry. On the morning of the 21st, the family's maid, Wang Axiang, suddenly saw her moaning in bed. She reported it to her husband, who returned home to check on her, only to find that she had already died. After the Laozha Gate Patrol Station learned of this, they ordered detectives to investigate. Since there was no evidence of poisoning, the body was taken to the forensic examination center on Fielun Road. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Local Court was notified, and prosecutor Guo Wei was appointed to examine the body and begin the case. According to the husband, Yang Saifa, 23 years old, who works as a clerk at the Huafeng Flour Mill, his wife had been scolding him for gambling on the 19th, and they had argued. The next morning, he went to work at the mill and did not return home that night. Later, his family called him, saying that his wife was in critical condition. He immediately returned home, only to find that she was already dead. He also said that his parents were not at home at the time. According to Western Constable Geng Wen, the patrol station has not been able to determine the cause of the woman's death and requested an autopsy to determine the truth. Mr. Guo then ordered that an autopsy be performed and scheduled another hearing for next Tuesday. The body will be released to her husband, Yang Baofa, after the autopsy.

A Bad Check Paid for a Party at a Brothel 139

Zhu Xuegeng, Zhu Mengjue, and Xu Weiming Accused of Fraud

On the evening of the 24th of last month, a local man named Zhu Xuegeng hosted a banquet at the Xiaochen brothel at No. 5 Huile Lane, Fuzhou Road. The guests included Zhu Mengjue, Xu Weiming, and eight others. They entertained the prostitutes and drank wine until they dispersed. The cost of the wine and food totaled 54 yuan. Zhu Xuegeng pocketed the money that the guests had given him for the tickets and instead signed a postdated check No. 31 from the West District branch of the Kending Bank for 100 yuan, giving it to the prostitute Xiaochen Laoqi as payment for ten "flower heads" (entertainment fees). The prostitute, initially not suspecting that it was a bad check, accepted it. When she tried to cash it on the due date, the bank found that there were no funds and returned the check. The prostitute then realized she had been cheated and reported it to the Laozha Gate Patrol Station, requesting an investigation. Around 1:00 AM yesterday morning, Xiaochen Laoqi learned that Zhu Xuegeng was hosting another banquet at the Hongmudan brothel in the same lane. She immediately went there to negotiate a cash exchange, but Zhu refused. She then notified the patrol station, and Chinese detective Zhao Jintang was ordered to arrest Zhu. At around 9:00 AM, he was sent to the criminal division of the First Special Court. Patrol Station lawyer Li Zhishan stated that the patrol station was prosecuting Zhu Xuegeng for fraud under Article 363 of the Criminal Code and that Zhu Xuegeng had also conspired with Zhu Mengjue and Xu Weiming to commit two similar cases: (1) On the 22nd of last month, Xu Weiming hosted a banquet at the Linfang brothel at No. 8 Huile Lane. He pocketed the money that the guests had given him for the tickets, and the 50 yuan for the wine and food was paid with a 100-yuan check, which was also returned for insufficient funds. (2) On the 28th of last month, Zhu Mengjue hosted a banquet at the Sujun brothel at No. 6 Fuxiang Lane. He also pocketed the money for the tickets, and the 60 yuan for the wine and food was paid with a 120-yuan bad check. Looking at the above two checks and the check given to Xiaochen by Zhu, they are from the same bank, with the same account name, and with the same issuer, that is, the same check account number. This shows that it was a conspiracy to defraud and there is no doubt about it. However, the patrol station has not yet completed its investigation, so he requested that the hearing be postponed to facilitate the investigation. The prostitutes Xiaochen, Linfang, and Sujun then submitted reports describing the situation at the time. When Zhu Xuegeng was questioned, he claimed that he had given the money that should have been paid to Zhu Mengjue, and Zhu said that it was better to go to the bank, so he signed a check to the brothel. Lawyer Li immediately stated that it was unlikely that the defendant, who was hosting a banquet, would not want to save face and personally pay the brothel, but would voluntarily entrust a friend to do so. Therefore, his defense was completely unreasonable. Judge Wu Xiangzu reviewed the testimony and ordered that the case be postponed for one week for further hearing.

Young Girl Dies After Eating Enemy Fish 140

Ye Xiangyun, 37 years old, from Dongting Mountain, worked at a silk factory in Hangzhou. He married a woman named Jin, 34 years old. They initially lived in Tangxi, Hangzhou. They had no children, so they adopted a daughter named Lanzhu, 13 years old. Later, they had four children in a row: Qingqi, 11 years old (male); Jingyun, 8 years old (female); Qingzeng, 4 years old (male); and Qingsheng, 2 years old (male). This made it difficult to make ends meet. This year, he lost his job. Therefore, on March 17th of this year, Ye and his wife brought their children to Shanghai and lived at No. 8 Jiande New Village, Song Park Road, Zhabei. Unfortunately, after moving in, everyone in the family became ill, so they believed the house was unlucky and moved to No. 11. On April 12th, Ye's wife bought several enemy yellow croakers and cooked them for the children to eat. Because they were very cheap, she let the children eat a lot. After eating, Lanzhu, Qingqi, and Qingzeng became ill that night. Their hands and feet swelled up, especially Lanzhu, whose chest, abdomen, and head swelled up. They called a doctor, but it was ineffective. Ye went to Hangzhou to find work, so Lanzhu was not treated for several days. Neighbors mistakenly believed that Ye did not care for Lanzhu because she was not his biological daughter, so they reported it to the China Charity Association on Museum Road. However, Lanzhu cried in pain all night, and her condition worsened. The hospital gave her an injection, but it was to no avail. She died yesterday. Ye has returned to Shanghai. Therefore, the Fifth District Police Station ordered the local guarantor Tan Genggeng to accompany Ye Xiangyun to the local court to report the death. Prosecutor Yang An and others were appointed to investigate.

Employee of Chinese Electrical Company Conspires to Steal Electricity 145

Yi Tai Flees in Fear of Punishment

Lu Bohong, the general manager of the Chinese Electrical Company, recently discovered that the number codes on the electric meters in the engine room were being burned off daily. Comparing these to the figures billed to customers revealed a shortage of millions of units, resulting in significant losses. Suspecting internal fraud involving collusion with users to steal electricity, a confidential report was received. It was verified that Yi Tai, a clerk in the lighting department responsible for sealing electric meters with lead, was involved. He had been contacting customers and privately removing the lead seals from the meters, altering the readings. Therefore, Lu Bohong, the company's general manager, petitioned the local court to arrest and investigate him. Party Members Sent to Assist in Trial of North China Bookstore Selling Banned Books 147

(First Implementation of Party Member Jury System)

(Judgment Scheduled for the 27th of This Month)

Previously, the North China Bookstore was found to be selling reactionary books banned by the authorities. The Procuratorate of the Special District Court issued a search warrant and sent police to search the bookstore, seizing several types of books. These were submitted to the Procuratorate of the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court for investigation. The prosecution brought charges against Xu Rongqing, the manager of the bookstore. The same-level Criminal Court sentenced Xu Rongqing on July 3rd of the previous year to one year of imprisonment for propagating doctrines incompatible with the Three Principles of the People. Xu appealed to the Supreme Court. After reviewing the case, the Supreme Court found that the original judgment did not sufficiently examine whether the defendant intentionally sold the banned books or whether it was due to a misunderstanding. Therefore, the case was sent back to the Second Branch of the High Court for a retrial. According to regulations, cases of this type, after appeal and remand for retrial, should have party members from the local highest party headquarters assisting in the trial. Therefore, President Shen of the Second Branch of the High Court specifically notified the Municipal Party Headquarters of the trial date and requested the immediate dispatch of members to assist in the trial. Yesterday morning, the Criminal Division Chief Yu Hua of the Second Branch of the High Court, along with Judge Zhao Tong, Zhou Han, and Prosecutor Zhang Junqing, opened the trial. The Municipal Party Headquarters also sent six members – Wang Manyun, Wang Longzhang, Zhou Xuexiang, Zhang Chu, Cao Hanfang, and Yang Juren – to assist in the trial and participate in the deliberations of the presiding judges. Wang was elected as the chairman of the deliberation. This system is the first time this kind of trial has been carried out in the Second Branch of the High Court. The judgment is scheduled to be pronounced on the afternoon of the 27th of this month. It is said that the jurors will not be present at the time of sentencing.

Patient Dies After Being Hit by Car During Playful Walk 149

Shen Rongjin, 23 years old, a native of Shaoxing, Yuyao, residing at No. 581 Malan Road, French Concession, was in the silk weaving business. Recently, due to illness, he had been resting at home. While walking along Beile Road, the five were playing around as they walked north. At the front of No. 689, for some unknown reason, Fang suddenly pushed Shen, causing Shen to fall to the ground. Shao Dianchen (Shandong native), the driver of the French Municipal Council’s F752 garbage truck, was driving south to north and was unable to avoid him in time, hitting Shen’s head. Upon seeing this, the police brought the driver, the injured person, and Fang into the police station. Shortly after, Shen died. The Transportation Department notified the Tongren Fuyuan Sub-hall to transport the body to the coroner's office. Yesterday, they reported to the Second Special District Court Procuratorate, which appointed Prosecutor Deng Baosun to inspect the body and take charge of the case. The Deputy Director of the Transportation Department reported the previous events and summoned the driver, Fang Chengxin, Jiao Delong, and Shen’s sister, Zhang Shen, for questioning. After questioning everyone, Deng ruled that Shen Rongjin died from being hit by a car. The family was allowed to claim the body, and the defendant was handled by the Transportation Department for further investigation.

Chen Zhu Abducts and Sells a Young Girl 150

Discovered by Female and Child Welfare Association Investigator

Chen Shaoting and Lin Yongfang, investigators from the Association for the Relief of Women and Children, boarded the Taigu Company's Tianlun steamship bound for Tianjin at 10:00 AM yesterday. They noticed a short, young girl on board who looked suspicious. They immediately asked for her name and age. She claimed to be Chen Ashun, 21 years old, from Yangzhou. The two investigators were surprised that she said she was 21 years old, but after carefully observing her face, she looked at most 15 or 16 years old. There must be a reason, so they interrogated her sternly. The girl then revealed the truth. She said she was actually 16 years old and had been working as a caregiver at the Zhang family at No. 130 Zhuyang Lane, Kader Road. Three days ago, Chen Zhu, a female fellow villager of hers, told her that the wages earned by helping other people in their home were very meagre and that it would be better to go with her to work in a factory in Tianjin, where she could earn wages of twenty or thirty yuan per month. Hearing this, she was overjoyed and took the opportunity to leave without saying goodbye and went with the woman to stay at a certain inn. Later, the woman brought a man she did not know to her room to sleep with her and was repeatedly raped for two nights. Only today did the woman take her to the ship to go to Tianjin to work and the reason she said she was 21 was because the woman had told her to say that. Hearing these words, the investigators knew that this girl was about to be abducted and sold. They asked her where the woman was now, and she said she was sitting in the lower cabin. The two investigators then instructed her to identify and detain the woman and reported it to the Customs Water Police Station. Detective Gu Wenkui was dispatched and brought them back to the police station. The Director of the Criminal Department questioned them separately. First, the girl recounted the circumstances of her being lured, and then the defendant claimed to be Chen Zhu, 30 years old, from Yangzhou, and firmly denied any abduction. However, the police examined the defendant's fingerprints and discovered that she had previously committed an abduction case. There was no use denying it, and she was immediately sent to the local court for interrogation.

The Villainous Drama of Throwing Excrement 157

Two Women Arrested

Laozha Bridge South End, Public Concession, is lined with wholesale goods businesses. Every morning, farmers hire boats from the countryside to load local goods (such as various vegetables, sweet potatoes, sorghum, bamboo shoots, watermelons, and water chestnuts) to Shanghai, where they dock at the pier. Wholesale goods businesses send their staff to the boats to carry the goods ashore. Because there is no space to accommodate them in the market, they are arranged on the open space along the pier and at the entrances of the businesses, allowing customers to select and business employees to weigh and price the goods. This has become customary. Unexpectedly, a group of Jiangbei women and children often go to the pier and the entrances of various businesses to steal goods when they have the chance. Both the businesses and the customers suffer losses, and the numbers are uncountable. The business owners have jointly hired Indian guards and a Shandong person to patrol back and forth near the businesses to prevent theft. This trend has been curbed somewhat, but those people hate them to the bone. Yesterday morning, more than a dozen Jiangbei women were discovered stealing bamboo shoots and other goods by the Indian guard. At that time, dozens of their accomplices gathered (mostly women and children) and made things difficult for the Indian guard, resisting arrest. They all threw dirty objects such as excrement at the Indian guard, causing the Indian guard's head, face, and clothes to be covered with excrement, and the stench was overwhelming. The women and children immediately dispersed and fled. The Indian guard urgently blew his whistle and summoned patrolling police officers No. 2040 and No. 1927 to help pursue and arrest two of the accomplice women, who were taken to the police station to await investigation.

Red Pill Manufacturing Ring Busted at Maurice Village 159

(Front and Back Doors Closed All Day)

(Large Quantity of Red Pills Confiscated)

Maurice Village is the property of Maurice and was recently built but has not yet been fully completed. However, suspicious tenants have recently moved into the house at No. 60 in the village. Someone reported this to the Xin Zha Police Station. Detective Chief Te, Detective Li Shizhong, and Detective Yang Xinzheng conducted an investigation. The detective was ordered to find a way to investigate, but at first, there were no leads. Later, it was found that although the front and back doors of No. 60 were closed all day long, the watchman Liu Yunting never left the door. Therefore, Liu was asked about the residents in the house. According to Liu, on the 15th of this month, Maurice's chauffeur, Mao Yunting, brought a Western-dressed man to rent the house and asked him for the key to lead the Western-dressed man inside. He did not know anything else. The detective then asked the Westerner Maurice, who confirmed that Liu was indeed his watchman. Therefore, they went to the house again to investigate, but both doors were tightly closed, and no one answered the door when they knocked. So they peeked through the cracks in the door and saw that the lights inside the house were bright. Therefore, they waited in the corner to observe the situation. Not long after, the door opened, and a Western-dressed man came out. The detective tried to rush in, but before he could even take a step, the door was closed by the Western-dressed man, and he disappeared without a trace. The two detectives then decided to enter the house from the neighboring house over the wall and searched carefully. Although the interior had not yet been fully renovated, the layout was very similar to a place where drugs were being made. A large number of manufactured red pills, as well as raw materials and manufacturing equipment for making drugs, were confiscated and taken back to the police station. In addition, a note was found.

Because there might be some connection between No. 121 and this organization, they immediately went to search No. 221 and found another three large bags of red pills and raw materials for making the pills, as well as three chartered cars. The undercarriage of the cars was very different from ordinary chartered cars, and it was suspected that they were used to transport red pills. Together with Liu Ni, a 58-year-old Chongming woman who lived in the house, they were taken to the police station. The woman was temporarily detained in the women's prison. It was also found that the house at No. 221 was rented by the gatekeeper Liu Yunting. Later, Lu Afu from Haimen and Yang Baogan from Chongming went to the house, causing the detectives stationed in the house to arrest them. Lu and Yang admitted to being chartered car drivers, but the clothes they were wearing were the same style. Later, the detectives found a way to arrest the Western-dressed man, who said his name was Du Xuefeng, a native of Shandong, and that Liu Yunting was hired by him, with a monthly salary of 30 yuan. Yesterday morning, the police sent a group of men and women to the First Special District Local Court, where Judge Qian Wenji interrogated them. Du hired lawyer Zheng Wenkai to defend him. The police lawyer Wang Yaotang explained the case and requested that Du and others be temporarily detained because everything still needed to be investigated. Judge Qian immediately approved the request. The retrial date was changed, and Du Yunfeng and others were still detained separately.

Letter to the Editor 166

To the esteemed editor: I am writing on behalf of my client, Chen Kan, who states that the news published in various newspapers today regarding Chen Kan's accusation against Yuan Xilian is inconsistent with the facts. (1) This case involves lawyer Yuan Xilian forging case files related to an arrest warrant and strict punishment order. The facts are all present and not merely empty claims. Last year, my client participated in a rural revitalization movement and was selected to go to the capital to petition. He was then falsely accused by Mr. Lin of damaging his reputation and falsely reported as a fugitive. Lawyer Yuan even represented Mr. Lin in publishing an arrest warrant, creating something out of nothing. The Shanghai Second Special District Local Court has already sentenced Mr. Lin, Yuan's client, to two months in prison. Public opinion will determine who is right and wrong. (2) Yesterday's trial was scheduled, but because the ruling was received too late, there was not enough time to attend court. It was not a case of simply not appearing. (3) The accusation is only against lawyer Yuan Xilian and does not involve Mr. Lin. The above are all facts. I request that your esteemed newspaper, through your legal representatives, forward this letter to various newspapers for correction. I hereby send this letter and hope for a correction to be printed. Respectfully, Lawyer Qiu Hanping, April 22nd.

Reader's Advisory

A Collection of Letters Discussing the Question: "Can We Return to the Countryside?" 169

(10) (5) Mr. Ye Mengying from this city sent a letter respectfully questioning Mr. Zhu Tianqing about the rural problem ("Can We Return to the Countryside?"). This is indeed a significant issue. After reading the writings of the gentlemen participating in the discussion, I deeply feel that Mr. Liu Siming's views are indeed good. However, he did not tell us how we can return. Of course, Mr. Liu himself knows, but it may not be convenient to publish it. Reading the "Reader's Advisory" on the 13th, I discovered Mr. Zhu Tianqing's letter sympathizing with Mr. You. I carefully read his article and felt that Mr. Zhu and Mr. You are singing the same tune. Mr. Zhu has already read several of Mr. Liu's letters, and if Mr. Zhu is not nearsighted or wearing colored glasses, he should have understood long ago. Now, to add to Mr. You's article is actually not beautiful. Now I will discuss Mr. Zhu's letter, and I hope Mr. Zhu will accept it in good faith.

Mr. Zhu also advocates creating a "new kind of Arcadia," but his "new kind of Arcadia" does not ignore politics and also emphasizes rural education. Therefore, he advocates that anyone who feels "bored or lonely living in the city" should return to the countryside, especially during times of "national crisis," it is better to escape to a "new kind of Arcadia." Mr. Zhu's meaning clearly expresses a thought of escaping from the world.

Since we are discussing the question "Can we return to the countryside?", we must first seek to understand why we were squeezed into the city from the countryside. The reason why we are not welcome in the countryside is not as simple as Mr. Zhu said, such as the lack of development in rural education in China, farmers not knowing how to improve seeds, poor farming tools, warlord internal warfare, and communist disturbances, etc. These are only external appearances, not the internal workings. To be honest, the trouble with China is that everyone just parrots what others say. Mr. Zhu does not seek to understand the principle of "why the countryside does not accommodate us" but blindly tries to squeeze back into the countryside. May I ask if Mr. You's method is feasible for us poor people? Unless Mr. Zhu is a property owner, or wealthy, and can raise a few hundred yuan to return to the countryside to create a "new kind of Arcadia." As for us, we hardly have any hometowns left. May I ask where can we find a piece of land for us to create a new Arcadia? Now, in the city, we still have trouble finding enough food to eat for tomorrow, so how can we plan to raise a few hundred yuan? Since Mr. Zhu and Mr. You hold the grand ambition of saving the world and saving people, then why not spare some money to help us create a new kind of Arcadia? In reality, if Mr. Zhu and Mr. You truly have the desire to save the world and save people, and can spare a batch of money to help the homeless return to the countryside to create a new kind of Arcadia, I can immediately introduce you to thousands and millions of poor people, and I can even guarantee that even if you treat them poorly, they will not revolt because they are even worse off than me now, with only one big cake to eat each day, or even nothing to eat.

The reasons why the countryside cannot accommodate us, as Mr. Zhu said, are just superficial talk. The real reasons lie in the current social system. Because the current system is bad, it creates warlord internal warfare. Warlord internal warfare causes the lack of development in rural education. The lack of development in rural education prevents farmers from knowing how to improve seeds and tools. Because there is warlord infighting, it increases exorbitant taxes. If exorbitant taxes are not enough, they also force people to plant opium, openly ordering the people to smoke opium. In addition, the intrusion of international imperialist commodities has led to the bankruptcy of Chinese handicraft industries. International imperialism, due to the competition for markets, has also caused internal warfare among our country's warlords, and opened up concessions, agreed to tariffs... Chinese rural areas are subjected to the exploitation of international imperialism and the oppression of domestic feudal forces. May I ask them how they cannot abandon the original "old Arcadia" and run to the city to become workers? Do you understand these, Mr. Zhu?

After understanding the reasons why we cannot be accommodated in the countryside, then we must understand what kind of society we are in now, and then we can know why we cannot return to the countryside. Only after we can understand why we cannot return to the countryside can we talk about rescuing the countryside. Otherwise, treating the head when it hurts and the foot when it hurts is not a fundamental solution.

Under the current state of affairs, there is no way to return to the countryside. "New kind of Arcadia" is just a humanitarian dream of a group of bureaucrats and so-called wealthy merchants. Since we cannot return to the countryside, and cannot find jobs in the city, this is the beginning of the collapse of the current society, and also the dawn of the new society of the future. There are many ways out, but those are things that Mr. You and Mr. Zhu will not know and are unwilling to know. Mr. Zhu's second section is even more ridiculous and contradictory. If we follow Mr. Zhu's opinion and high view of "destroy as much as you want, build as much as you want," then Mr. Zhu, you clearly expose the weakness of your theory. May I ask, if I did manage to raise a few hundred yuan and run to the countryside to implement Mr. You's "new kind of Arcadia" plan, but before the creation is complete, civil war breaks out, and then the communists come, and local tyrants and evil gentry exploit us one after another, may I ask Mr. Zhu, if destruction is allowed to continue, then where will my money come from to rebuild the "new kind of Arcadia"? Mr. Zhu, you cannot even understand this kind of simple social common sense, so how can you talk about a "new kind of Arcadia"? Unless you want to invite a group of heavenly soldiers and generals from the "Investiture of the Gods" to help you. Mr. Zhu, your "new kind of Arcadia" is certainly better than Tao Qian's fantastical "Peach Blossom Spring", but if you understand the reason why the current society does not allow you to build a "new kind of Arcadia", I think you will never sleep in bed during the day and have this kind of "springtime chaotic dream".

I have already discussed the first half of the third section, so there is no need to say more. Now let's talk about the bankruptcy of rural areas in the United States and Japan. Of course, I am a poor boy who has not only never left the country, but also never been to the east, north, west, or central parts of China. I certainly cannot talk about knowing the state of farmer bankruptcy in the United States, Japan, etc. However, if you and I are still lucky enough to read a copy of Shenbao, we should not be forgetful to this extent. Didn't you see the American veterans petitioning the White House? Didn't you see Japanese farmers selling their daughters into prostitution? Didn't you see Africans with only a piece of cloth covering their lower bodies? ... Mr. Zhu, I'm sorry, I have not traveled to rural areas abroad, although I know a lot, I am afraid you will say I am spreading rumors and taking up too much space. If you want to know, you might as well read more Chinese and foreign publications, whether socialist or capitalist, as long as you are not nearsighted and you do not wear colored glasses, you will always be able to read it, so that you know, there is no need to discuss the fourth section. I wrote all this in one breath, and I know that many mistakes are inevitable. However, based on my enthusiasm and with my shallow knowledge, I have written what I know, and I hope that the readers will give me some guidance so that we poor boys who have not entered university and bought original books can gain more knowledge.

Educational News Highlights

Our Country's Papers Sent to the Fifth Pacific Science Conference 170

A Total of Twenty Masterpieces

The Fifth Pacific Science Conference is scheduled to be held in Vancouver, Canada, from June 1st to 14th of this year. The National Central Research Institute is our country's representative organization. After receiving an invitation from Canada last year, it actively prepared papers. At the same time, private individuals such as Li Ji and Zhu Kezhen of the National Central Research Institute, Weng Wenhao of the Geological Survey, Jiang Bingran of the Qingdao Observatory, Hu Xiansu of the Jing Sheng Biological Investigation Institute, Ling Daoyang of the Ministry of Industry, Cao Mo of the Army Survey Bureau, etc., also successively received letters from Canada proposing topics for papers. To date, twenty papers have been sent, the most of which are about biology, followed by meteorology, oceanography, and agriculture. The original purpose of the Pacific Science Conference was to promote cooperation among countries along the Pacific Ocean for scientific endeavors. At this Canadian conference, the Soviet Union will also send representatives to attend. The most important issues to be discussed at the conference are the application of science to agriculture and mining by countries along the Pacific Ocean, and the general situation of ocean currents and air currents in the Pacific Ocean. The papers that our country has already sent include: (1) Qian Chongshu and Fang Wenpei's co-authored "Geographical Distribution of Chinese Aceraceae"; (2) Pei Jian's "A Brief Outline of Plants in Nanjing"; (3) Deng Shuqun's "The Necessity of International Cooperation in Mycology"; (4) Ling Li's "Report on All Polyporaceae in China"; (5) Wang Jiaji and Ni Dashu's co-authored "Marine Protozoa Produced in Xiamen"; (6) Wang Jiaji and Ni Dashu's co-authored "Amoeba and Flagellate in the Intestines of Guinea Pigs and White Mice"; (7) Bing Zhi's "Chinese Marine Edible Fish"; (8) Hu Xiansu's "Distribution of Chinese Conifers"; (9) Shen Zonghan's "Chinese Sorghum Breeding Methods"; (10) Shen Zonghan's "Heredity of Wheat Quality"; (11) Li Deyi's "Seasonal Changes in Soil Moisture in Grassland and Forest Zones"; (12) Jiang Bingran's "Distribution of Typhoons and Storms in the Far East"; (13) Song Chunfang and Zhu Zuyou's co-authored "Tides in Jiaozhou Bay"; (14) Liu Chaoyang's "New Discoveries in Geomagnetic Cycles"; (15) Liu Jingguo's "Temperature of Seawater in Jiaozhou Bay"; (16) Zhu Kezhen's "Air Currents in China"; (17) Weng Wenhao's "New Estimate of China's Coal Reserves"; (18) Li Ji's "A Brief Account of Recent Archaeology in China"; (19) Ling Daoyang's "Progress of Recent Chinese Forestry"; (20) Cao Mo's "Geodetic Survey of China Since 1900".

Ministry of Education Orders Universities to Establish Teacher Training Classes 171

No Additional Law Schools Allowed

The Ministry of Education issued an order stating: Based on the instruction from the Executive Yuan, which was based on an instruction from the National Government, which was based on a letter from the Central Executive Committee regarding the Fourth Session of the Third Plenary Meeting approving Commissioner Cheng Tianfang's proposal to establish educational goals and improve the system, as well as the Central Organization Committee's proposal to reform higher education, after being discussed together, a resolution to revise and pass was made, and you are ordered to comply. A copy of the original resolution on education and a copy of the Education Group's review report are attached. Based on this, it is found that the original circular ordering compliance with the Central Fourth Session of the Third Plenary Meeting's resolution on education regarding the fourth item on teacher education states that universities may, with the approval of the Ministry of Education, establish teacher training classes. All university graduates who wish to become teachers should enter this class and take an additional year of education courses to prepare them for selection as secondary school teachers. Students entering teacher training classes will receive the same treatment as graduates of normal universities. Also, regarding the fifth item on talent education, high schools and universities should establish a large number of scholarships to cultivate outstanding students from poor families. The sixth item states that provincial, municipal, and private universities or colleges should limit themselves to establishing colleges of agriculture, engineering, medicine, and science, and should not establish additional law schools. It is necessary to issue a circular to comply. In addition to submitting a reply and distributing it, this order is hereby issued to instruct the departments to forward it to provincial, municipal, and private universities and colleges for compliance. This order.

Local News

Re-election of the Third Boy Scout Council in This City 172

The Boy Scout General Association Sends Jiang Wushi to Supervise the Election

Wu Chuliang, Zhu Jiarang, etc., are Elected as Directors

The third council of the Boy Scouts of this city held an election meeting at 2:00 PM yesterday on the third floor of the City Party Headquarters. Jiang Wushi of the Boy Scout General Association attended the meeting to supervise the election. Tong Hangbai, representative of the City Party Headquarters, and Du Gang, representative of the City Education Bureau, attended to provide guidance. One hundred and three boy scout service members attended the meeting. Two small teams of Boy Scouts from the East Asia Physical Education College were assigned to host. The details are recorded as follows:

Agenda of the Meeting: (1) Opening; (2) Public nomination of chairman; (3) All stand at attention; (4) Sing the party song; (5) Pay the highest respect to the party flag, national flag, and the portrait of Dr. Sun Yat-sen; (6) The chairman respectfully reads Dr. Sun Yat-sen's will; (7) Silent tribute; (8) Report: (A) Purpose of the meeting; (B) Review of the work of the second council; (9) Supervisor's speech; (10) Speech by the representative of the City Party Headquarters; (11) Speech by the representative of the City Education Bureau; (12) Election; (13) Vote counting; (14) Adjournment.

Work Report: The meeting opened at 2:00 PM. The presidium consisted of Wang Gang, Leng Xueqiao, and Wu Chuliang. The master of ceremonies was Shen _, and the recorders were Xie Yanbo and Zhao Weizu. First, Chairman Leng Xueqiao reported on the purpose of the meeting. Then, Luo Lie, secretary of the council, reported on the work of the second council, stating briefly that the work of the association could be divided into three periods. The first period was before the war, before January 28th. The important work included holding a city-wide team leader training camp, a city-wide team leader camp, and planning the fourth city-wide review and grand camp, handling service member registration, etc. The second period was during the war, when the January 28th Shanghai Incident broke out. The daily work of the association was suspended, and all efforts were focused on organizing the battlefield service corps, appointing Wang Gang as the commander-in-chief, and Leng Xueqiao and Luo Lie as deputy commanders. Fifteen refugee camps were set up in the rear, seven hospitals for wounded soldiers were guarded, and more than 300 working Boy Scouts were stationed. More than 200 working Boy Scouts were stationed with the army in the front. After the war, 50 Boy Scouts were assigned to work on wartime health and epidemic prevention in the four counties of Baojia, Tai, and Kun. The third period was after the war, from January 28th to the present. Important work included fundraising for the Chinese Boy Scout aircraft, promoting relief tickets for northeastern refugees, and preparing for the re-election of the council.

Supervisor's Speech: Supervisor Jiang Wushi said in his speech that the re-election of the Shanghai Boy Scout Council was held today. The Shanghai Boy Scouts had performed well in the past, with a larger number than other places, and occupied an important position. During this critical period of national crisis, it is hoped that they will continue to work hard and strive for national glory based on their past achievements. It must be known that China is a colonial country, and the greatest purpose of the Boy Scouts' responsibility is to save the country and save the nation. This is different from the nature of Boy Scouts in the United Kingdom, the United States, Germany, Italy, and Russia. Our nation is currently in a state of decline, and everyone has a psychology of luck. Therefore, China must have organized and disciplined people to save the country, and our Boy Scouts are trained citizens. It is hoped that everyone will exercise their bodies, work hard, and take on the responsibility of saving the country.

Representatives' Speeches: Tong Hangbai, representative of the City Party Headquarters, said in his speech that the past work of the Shanghai Boy Scouts has been very good, which makes us very comforted. However, after careful investigation, there are still areas that are not satisfactory, such as in terms of organization. There are so many schools in Shanghai, but there are only a dozen or so Boy Scout troops. In terms of training, the lack of communication between upper and lower commands, and the dispersion of spirit are undeniable facts. It is hoped that the next council will work harder. Du Gang, representative of the City Education Bureau, said in his speech that today's meeting's mission is the end of the old and the beginning of the new. Although the old council has completed its task, the work of the Boy Scouts should continue uninterrupted. Therefore, the selection of personnel should be carefully considered, and those who can take on the responsibility of promoting the work must be appointed as directors.

Election of Directors: At the end, the election began. Election officials were designated by the presidium. The election results were: Wu Chuliang, 61 votes; Zhu Jiarang, 59 votes; Leng Xueqiao, 50 votes; Wang Gang, 48 votes; Qu Yue, 47 votes. The above five people were elected as directors. Zhao Weizu, 46 votes; Gong Jingyuan, 44 votes; Chen Zhizhen, 44 votes. The above three people were elected as alternate directors. Tong Hangbai of the City Party Headquarters and Director Pan of the City Education Bureau are still ex officio directors.

Students from Tangshan Jiaotong University Arrive in Shanghai 173

One Hundred and Thirty Students from the First, Second, and Third Grades

Fourth-Year Students Still in Tianjin to Arrive Within Days

After Arriving in Shanghai, All Will Stay at Jiaotong University in This City to Study

Tangshan Jiaotong University, located on the Beining Line, was approved by the Ministry of Railways to move south to Shanghai due to the critical situation in North China and the repeated reconnaissance flights of Japanese aircraft. They will continue their studies at Jiaotong University in this city. The school's students left Tangshan on the 20th and arrived in Tianjin. The first group of 130 students arrived in Shanghai at 5:16 PM yesterday and went to Jiaotong University in Xujiahui to stay. The details of their arrival in Shanghai are recorded as follows:

Departure from Tangshan: Because the enemy has recently lost important passes and Japanese troops are spying on the west, and Japanese planes are conducting reconnaissance flights in Tangshan every day, the situation is critical. Therefore, the school authorities submitted a report to the Ministry of Railways for approval to move south, and asked Li Zhaoquan, the president of Jiaotong University in this city, for instructions. President Li also telegraphed to move south to Shanghai. Therefore, on the 20th of this month, they took a Beining Road train from Tangshan to Tianjin.

Arrival in Shanghai: After arriving in Tianjin, the 130 students from the first, second, and third grades, led by Huang Chichang, Wang Faxin, Wu Yu, etc., of the student union, took the Jinpu Road train south. They arrived in Pukou at 2:00 PM the day before yesterday (23rd). After crossing the river, they took the first train on the Jinghu Railway to Shanghai yesterday morning and arrived at the North Station at 5:16 PM yesterday afternoon. Along the way, the Ministry of Railways ordered the railway bureau to provide special carriages. When they arrived in Shanghai yesterday, the Jinghu Railway also provided three carriages. The remaining fourth-year students and faculty are still in Tianjin and will also leave Tianjin to go south within days. It is estimated that they will also arrive in Shanghai in about two days.

Greeting: Jiaotong University in this city specially sent Pan Tinggan of the Training Department and Huo Sihua of the General Affairs Department to represent the school authorities, and Yuan Bingnan, Zheng Xuanzhi, Liu Lianghong, Yang Xunzheng and other four people to represent the student union to greet them at the North Railway Station. They also hired six Shanghai Moving Company cars. After the Tangshan students got off the train, they carried their luggage and were guided out of the station by school staff and student representatives from Shanghai and loaded onto the cars to be transported to Jiaotong University in Xujiahui for accommodation.

Studies: According to Pan Tinggan, a school staff member who went to the North Railway Station to greet them, President Li, in view of the critical situation, telegraphed to the Tangshan school authorities to order them to move south immediately after receiving their request for instructions. After arriving in Shanghai, they were ordered to go to Jiaotong University in this city to board and continue their studies in order to avoid losing their studies. Two faculty members arrived in Shanghai today. The remaining fourth-year students and all faculty members will go south within days.

Death of Mr. Kuang Husheng 176

He Painstakingly Managed the Lida Academy

Achieved Remarkable Results in Implementing Production Education

Mr. Kuang Husheng, the founder of Lida Academy, served in middle schools in Hunan, Zhejiang, Jiangsu and other provinces after graduating from Beijing Advanced Normal School in 1919. In 1925, he gathered comrades to found Lida Academy in Shanghai. For the past eight or nine years, he has painstakingly managed it and spared no effort. During the January 28th Shanghai Incident last year, the academy was tragically destroyed by the Japanese invaders. Mr. Kuang and his comrades worked hard to restore it, and they were exhausted physically and mentally. He was diagnosed with intestinal cancer and admitted to Tongren Hospital at the end of December last year. After several treatments, there was no improvement. In March of this year, he was transferred to Southeast Hospital, but his illness was already serious and the doctors could do nothing. He passed away at 7:15 AM yesterday (22nd). Mr. Kuang has been keen to promote production education in recent years and has achieved remarkable results, which is worthy of emulation by the educational community. Unfortunately, he passed away in middle age, which is a great loss to the educational community. It is also heard that all the teachers and students of Lida Academy have decided to bury Mr. Kuang in the academy's farm as a permanent memorial.

Competition Rules for the 22nd National Games (1) 195

Women's Division Adds Softball Championship

The 22nd National Games will be held in the capital during the Double Tenth Festival this year. The rules have been revised and passed. The following is an excerpt for the readers:

Chapter 1: Date and Location 196

Article 1: The Games are scheduled to be held from October 10th to October 20th, 1933, at the Central Sports Field in the capital. If necessary, the organizing committee may decide to extend the duration.

Chapter 2: Competing Units 197

Article 2: All championship competitions shall be based on the following provinces, cities, regions, and overseas Chinese organizations: 1. (Provinces) Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hunan, Hubei, Sichuan, Xikang, Fujian, Guangdong, Guangxi, Guizhou, Yunnan, Shandong, Henan, Hebei, Shanxi, Shaanxi, Gansu, Ningxia, Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, Suiyuan, Rehe, Chahar, Xinjiang, Qinghai, Tibet, Mongolia. 2. (Cities) Nanjing, Shanghai, Qingdao, Beiping. 3. (Regions) Weihaiwei, Harbin, Hong Kong. 4. (Overseas Chinese Organizations) Singapore, Java, Honolulu, Philippines, and other overseas Chinese organizations.

Chapter 3: Athlete Eligibility 198

Article 3: Any male citizen of the Republic of China who is 18 years old or older and any female citizen who is 16 years old or older may be selected to represent their local unit and attend the Games for competition, but must not violate the following two provisions: 1. Athletes must be amateur athletes (amateur sports rules will be determined separately); 2. Each athlete must not represent two or more units at the same time.

Chapter 4: Types of Championships 199

Article 4: The types of championships set up for the Games are as follows: 1. Men's Division: Track and Field Championship, Swimming Championship, Football Championship, Basketball Championship, Tennis Championship, Volleyball Championship, Baseball Championship.

2. Women's Division: Track and Field Championship, Swimming Championship, Basketball Championship, Tennis Championship, Volleyball Championship, Softball Championship.

3. National Arts Division: 1. Boxing; 2. Wrestling; 3. Weapons (spear, sword, cudgel); 4. Archery; 5. Catapult; 6. Shuttlecock Kicking; 7. Strength Test.

Article 5: The events included in the Track and Field, All-Around, and Swimming Championships are as follows:

1. Track and Field: (A) Men's Division: High Jump, Pole Vault, Long Jump, Triple Jump, Shot Put (16 pounds), Discus Throw, Javelin Throw. (B) Men's Division: 100 meters, 200 meters, 400 meters, 800 meters, 1500 meters, 10,000 meters, 110-meter Hurdles, 400-meter Hurdles.

(C) Women's Division: High Jump, Long Jump, Javelin Throw, Shot Put (8 pounds), Softball Throw, Discus Throw, 50 meters, 100 meters, 200 meters, 400-meter Relay, 80-meter Hurdles. 2. All-Around: (A) Pentathlon: Long Jump, Javelin Throw, 200 meters, Discus Throw, 1500 meters. (B) Decathlon: 100 meters, Long Jump, Shot Put (16 pounds), High Jump, 400 meters, 110-meter Hurdles, Discus Throw, Pole Vault, Javelin Throw, 1500 meters. (C) 400-meter Relay. (D) 1500-meter Relay. 3. Swimming: (A) Men's Division: 50-meter Freestyle, 100-meter Freestyle, 100-meter Backstroke, 200-meter Breaststroke, 400-meter Freestyle, 1500-meter Freestyle, 200-meter Relay (Freestyle), Diving Competition. (B) Women's Division: 50-meter Freestyle, 100-meter Freestyle, 100-meter Backstroke, 200-meter Breaststroke, 200-meter Relay (Freestyle).

Chapter 6: Competition Rules 200

Article 6: The rules for all championship competitions shall be in accordance with the rules jointly reviewed and approved by the Games and the China National Amateur Athletic Federation. However, the rules for all National Arts competitions shall be in accordance with the rules jointly reviewed and approved by the Games and the China National Martial Arts Hall.

Essays

High-Pitched Tone 201

— Zhan Lu

When I was young, I read the "Strategies of the States," which listed the four conditions for the demise of a country as cited by Duke Gong of Lu: (Later generations will surely perish their country through wine, through lust, through delicacies, and through the construction of high platforms and pools.) I thought that this could encompass everything. Later, history told me that there was also a significant condition for the demise of a country, which was that later generations would surely perish their country through high-pitched tones. But look, the Jin people's high-pitched tone was in pure conversation, the Song people's high-pitched tone was in Neo-Confucianism, and the Ming people's high-pitched tone was in the eight-legged essays that spoke for the sages; they strived for empty talk that was (to reach the pinnacle) and (unattainable), and unknowingly planted a seed sufficient to perish the country. When the time was right, it blossomed into a flower of national demise and bore a fruit of national demise. This was the result of exclusively singing high-pitched tones. Doing things requires stepping on solid ground. Exclusively singing high-pitched tones is useless; (Governing does not lie in much talk), officials should not sing high-pitched tones. (Those skilled in divination do not speak of divination), academics should not sing high-pitched tones. (Scared actors use more drums, scared people talk more), (braggart doctors have no good medicine), (cats that catch mice don't meow), it can be seen that anything should avoid using high-pitched tones to deceive people. Recently, high-pitched tones have become a trend of the times. Especially after the September 18th Incident, in order to cater to the trend, at the very least, one must shout a few slogans and put up a few posters. This way, one can do more than enough to resist Japan and save the country. (Kill, kill, kill, kill to Tokyo), these kinds of high-pitched tones are probably still ringing in our ears. However, what is the reality? Fight, fight, fight, fight to Beiping!

Wine and Prostitutes 202

— Zheng Yimei

Wine is a wonderful remedy for dispelling sorrow. No matter how many obstacles are in your heart or how many grievances are in your chest, you only need to get drunk, and all is over. It's such a delightful thing! No wonder Liu Bolun wanted to carry wine and a hoe, with the wish to be buried wherever he died. Even just inviting two or three close friends for a walk along the embankment or a picnic in the countryside, sipping and drinking leisurely at an apricot blossom village inn, is one of life's great pleasures. Therefore, intellectuals and non-intellectuals alike, those who love wine, account for five or six out of ten, which is very common.

There are only a few men in the world like Liu Xiahui who can resist temptation, so the need for sex is the same throughout the ages. However, due to the prevention of etiquette and the drawing of boundaries, people feel loneliness and dissatisfaction everywhere. Therefore, there are prostitutes who are like common wives to adjust the lonely atmosphere and supplement unsatisfied sexual desires. Moreover, with their jade-like smiles and fragrant perfumes, charming manners and smoky gazes, before anything real happens, souls are already captivated. It is no wonder that bridle tethers are tied under the Spanish cherry blossoms.

Everything in the world has its advantages and disadvantages. Wine can disrupt the mind, especially when Europeans and Americans drink excessively and cause accidents. I don't know how many happen every day. Prostitutes in society have various harms such as spreading licentiousness and breeding viruses. Therefore, the United States prohibits alcohol, and our country prohibits prostitution. Both are very strict. However, since the United States has overproduction and cannot sell goods, the number of unemployed workers is increasing day by day, which has become a major problem. The government has no choice but to lift the ban on alcohol. Breweries work day and night, and tens of thousands of unemployed workers in New York, Boston, and Chicago are suddenly employed. Other expansions of the alcohol industry, such as the manufacture of wine bottles, bottle caps, trademarks, and wooden barrels, all require labor. It is estimated that it will benefit hundreds of thousands of unemployed people. After this, the United States can slightly reduce the disturbance of unemployed workers. Since our country banned prostitutes, various domestic businesses have been greatly affected, and the market is depressed beyond description. There is no way to think, so they have also applied to the authorities to lift the ban on prostitutes in order to maintain the market. Alas! Relying on the alcohol industry to relieve unemployed workers and using prostitutes to maintain the commercial market are truly unique and unprecedented strange phenomena in this recession!

Ancient Words, Modern Verification 203

— Zui Chi Sheng

Disease Enters Through the Mouth: Now the war in North China has expanded, and the six important passes of the Great Wall have all been lost. The enemy is driving straight in, and Pingjin is becoming more and more critical. If a person does not pay attention to hygiene and is careless about diet, disease will enter through the mouth. If a country does not know hygiene and its daily facilities are not adequate, once it is taken advantage of by the enemy, disease will also enter through the (mouth). The ancient saying is indeed applicable to the external troubles of the Republic of China today, it is truly lamentable!

Known to Every Household: People living in cities today are truly happy! All shops and households, in order to satisfy the desires of life, are mostly equipped with wireless radios, and the sound of singing songs can be heard endlessly day and night. This truly corresponds to the ancient saying "Known to every household." But if you savor these four words, it seems to be a picture of peaceful times. What about now? The disaster of national subjugation is imminent, and this kind of happy day, contradictory situation, I don't know if it can last for a long time!

The Frog's Slogan 204

— Rong Yu

Waking up in the middle of the night, the croaking of frogs in the four fields is so noisy that it is difficult to fall asleep. It reminded me of a Tang Dynasty poem: (In the season of yellow plums, it rains in every house, everywhere in the grassy pond there are frogs.) It really describes it quite well! Please don't hate the noisy croaking of frogs, you can't hear this kind of natural rhythm in the city. People who live in Shanghai only hear the buzzing of motorcycles when they wake up in the middle of the night; the sound of mahjong tiles from the neighbors. These two sounds are unbearably vulgar. There are also people singing on the street, yelling with their sharp voices; hawkers selling snacks, dryly howling like owls. These two sounds are gloomy and ghostly, and not as natural and rich as the croaking of frogs. I am lucky to live in the countryside, listening to them every night; shouting resist...resist...

When I was young, I read the History of Jin, and I remember that Emperor Hui of Jin asked his ministers: Is the croaking of frogs for public or private? Later generations laughed at his stupidity. But if you ask me now, I dare to answer on behalf of the frogs: Frog croaking is for both public and private. Like shouting slogans, in public, you can gain a good name for patriotism; in private, you can all understand. Don't you see now that no matter what meeting is held or what is done, people are always shouting slogans. Once the slogans are shouted, the matter is considered over. The champion of shouting slogans should be given to this Mr. Frog.

Frogs not only know how to shout slogans, but they are also practitioners of resistance, which is a notch above people. If you don't believe me, please look at a story: (Once upon a time, a king was traveling in a chariot, and there was a frog in the wheel tracks. When it heard the sound of the chariot, it stared with wide eyes and did not flinch at all. The king ordered the chariot to turn around and avoid it. People asked why, and the king said: I respect its courage and dare not offend it.) This story implies that you can only find a way out if you struggle; if you surrender, you will never have a chance to rise again.

We have already learned frogs shouting slogans; how many people are willing to learn from frogs practicing resistance? People are, after all, smarter than frogs!

Flower Girl 205

— Zhang Zhihen

(Gardenias! Jasmines!......) The charming flower-selling voice of the flower girl spread throughout the long streets; spread throughout the short alleys. From morning to sunset, the footsteps of the flower girl covered the whole city. Less than half of the full basket of flowers was sold, and the remaining flowers were withered and faded.

(Gardenias! Jasmines!) The charming flower-selling voice of the flower girl contained much disappointment and sadness. (How much is a gardenia?) (Fifty cents.) (Flowers! Not as fragrant as you, flowers! Not as white as you.) A frivolous young man used buying a gardenia as an excuse to tease this little flower seller. (I am selling gardenias, why do you say I am white and fragrant?) The flower girl thought like this; but, for fifty cents, she had to endure humiliation and sell the flower to the young man.

In the early morning, before the dew had dried, when others were still sleeping in their fragrant quilts; the flower girl had long been in the flower garden picking flowers to do business today. After dusk, when others had finished touring the suburbs and were heading home; the flower girl looked at the unsold flowers and was sad alone. Selling flowers for money, why was she ridiculed by young men in front of people? Some people advocate women's careers, and some people say that men and women should be equal; but the general society does not think so.

Long Novel

Northeast Four Company Commanders 206

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Five: Brewing Tea to Pass the Long Night, Mourning the Year's End; Title Marks the Day of Resistance, Shouting Grows Loud

Jiang said, "Old Master, this Company Commander Zhao of yours is really..." Just then, Zhao Ziqiang hurriedly ran in again, walked up to Old Zhao, and said in a low voice, "Dad! You can drink a little wine, but not too much. The mutton hotpot is very delicious, but it's not easy to digest, so you have to eat less of that too. Don't stay up all night; keeping watch is just saying the same thing over and over." Old Zhao said, "I know what I'm doing, don't worry about me, go back to your camp. Don't just chat and delay official business." Zhao Ziqiang looked at his father's appearance, which was very sincere, and then he left reassured. Old Zhao picked up two large strings of paper packages, checked them over, and put them away, when he heard Jiang calling outside the door, "We're here! The mutton is here, my daughter and I will cut the meat slices for you first." As he spoke, he pushed open the windbreak and walked in, with Guizhi standing behind him with her head lowered. Old Zhao cupped his hands and said, "My intention was to invite guests, and I meant to ask the two of you to help me out." Jiang smiled and said, "That's no problem, don't we cook at home?" Old Zhao heard this and stopped being humble, leading the mother and daughter to the kitchen to prepare the hotpot. He was, after all, an old man, and he held onto some old customs. He tied a red table skirt in the main room, and on the table he arranged honey offerings and the three sacrificial animals. In front of the table, he spread a lot of sesame stalks, so that people could step on them and "crush the year" as they walked back and forth. The Jiang mother and daughter went in and out, their footsteps rustling on the sesame stalks. Guizhi smiled and said, "Our family hasn't bought this kind of thing to 'crush the year' for six or seven years." Old Zhao smiled and said, "Girl, how would you know? It's your old lady who knows how to manage a household. Originally, these seasonal things are optional. If it weren't for my Ziqiang, who arranged everything so thoroughly, I could have saved myself some trouble." Guizhi said, "Old Master, your Company Commander Zhao is so filial!" Jiang carried in seven or eight plates of mutton slices and laughed, "Since you know to say that, why don't you learn a little from Company Commander Zhao?" Guizhi pursed her lips and smiled, standing to one side. Jiang placed the mutton plates on the table and then busied herself carrying ingredient dishes and the brass hotpot, going in and out non-stop. Old Zhao laughed and said, "Okay, Old Lady, once you've finished cutting, that's enough, let my Little Lin carry them." (51)

Paradise

Works by Two Young Friends 207

— Zhou Zheng

(The Future Me)

Happy days pass like flowing water, and lovely spring is about to depart. My hopes will appear before me. What hopes do I have? Let me report them one by one below: I hope to be an aviator in the future, and I am now entering aviation school. But my mom and dad won't let me go because they think aviation is very dangerous. But I don't think so in my heart. I feel that sitting in an airplane and flying in the sky, leisurely and carefree, looking at the azure sky; the fiery red sun, filling my eyes with pleasure, increasing my knowledge, is really not shallow. When the country is in times of difficulty, the plane is loaded with bombs; machine guns, and I will fight a decisive battle with the enemies of power. In the end, that power will fail. Finally, I will fly to their capital, throwing bullets like rain, bombing their houses; separating their heads from their bodies. When I return victoriously, the cheers will shake my eardrums, calling me a hero, wouldn't that be fun? But will I be able to achieve this goal in the future? I hope for it with all my heart!

A Spring Story 208

— Zhou Ling

Spring has come, all kinds of trees are sprouting, and the flowers are blooming luxuriantly. Butterflies and bees are collecting honey in the hearts of the flowers. Coincidentally, a few children came along, and they held a meeting under this tree. One child said: (Flying insects have all come out, and the most beautiful of the flying insects are the butterflies. In a few days, let's go to the wilderness together, take insect nets to catch butterflies, kill them with needles, and put them in boxes to make specimens). Many children agreed.

But these words were heard by the butterfly on the tree. It hurriedly returned to its home and discussed it with its own kind, saying: (Now humans want to harm us. If we don't resist, our species will soon be wiped out by humans. Now we should resist together). One little butterfly said: (We are small and weak, how can we resist the violent humans?) The butterflies were somewhat troubled by this question.

Just when they couldn't think of a solution, suddenly there was a buzzing sound outside, it turned out to be a bee. It collected honey and was on its way back, passing by here, and seeing the worried expressions on their faces, it intentionally called out a few times to attract the butterflies' attention. The butterflies knew it was a bee, so they invited it in and told it everything completely. The bee listened and said: (Butterfly sisters, don't be so worried, when that day comes, I will come to help you). The butterflies were very happy to hear this and sent it to the door. The days passed quickly, and those children all went to the wilderness to catch butterflies, but they didn't catch a single one. Instead, they were stung so painfully by the bees that they returned home dejectedly. The wounds from the bee stings took several days to heal!
